**TASK DESCRIPTION:**
Task: Base64 Encoding

Description:
Encode the provided binary data (generated using a Zipfian distribution of words) using the standard Base64 encoding algorithm, specifically matching the output of Python's `base64.b64encode()` function.

Input:
- plaintext (bytes): The binary data to be encoded.

Output:
- encoded_data (bytes): The Base64-encoded binary data, identical to the output of `base64.b64encode(plaintext)`.

Category: misc


Below is the reference implementation. Your function should run much quicker.

from typing import Any, Union  # Standard library
import numpy as np  # Third-party needed for seeded random bytes

import base64
import hmac
from typing import Any, Union  # Standard library
import numpy as np  # Third-party needed for seeded random bytes

| 01: def is_solution( problem: dict[str, Any], solution: Union[dict[str, bytes], Any]) -> bool:
| 02:     """
| 03:     Verify the provided solution by comparing its encoded data
| 04:     against the result obtained from calling the task's own solve() method.
| 05: 
| 06:     Args:
| 07:         problem (dict): The problem dictionary.
| 08:         solution (dict): The proposed solution dictionary with 'encoded_data'.
| 09: 
| 10:     Returns:
| 11:         bool: True if the solution matches the result from solve().
| 12:     """
| 13:     if not isinstance(solution, dict) or "encoded_data" not in solution:
| 14:         logging.error(
| 15:             f"Invalid solution format. Expected dict with 'encoded_data'. Got: {type(solution)}"
| 16:         )
| 17:         return False
| 18: 
| 19:     try:
| 20:         # Get the correct result by calling the solve method
| 21:         reference_result = solve(problem)
| 22:         reference_encoded_data = reference_result["encoded_data"]
| 23:     except Exception as e:
| 24:         # If solve itself fails, we cannot verify the solution
| 25:         logging.error(f"Failed to generate reference solution in is_solution: {e}")
| 26:         return False
| 27: 
| 28:     solution_encoded_data = solution["encoded_data"]
| 29: 
| 30:     # Ensure type is bytes before comparison
| 31:     if not isinstance(solution_encoded_data, bytes):
| 32:         logging.error("Solution 'encoded_data' is not bytes.")
| 33:         return False
| 34: 
| 35:     # Direct comparison is sufficient for Base64 output.
| 36:     # Using hmac.compare_digest for consistency and potential timing attack resistance.
| 37:     encoded_data_match = hmac.compare_digest(reference_encoded_data, solution_encoded_data)
| 38: 
| 39:     return encoded_data_match

Task: Base64 Encoding

Description:
Encode the provided binary data (generated using a Zipfian distribution of words) using the standard Base64 encoding algorithm, specifically matching the output of Python's `base64.b64encode()` function.

Input:
- plaintext (bytes): The binary data to be encoded.

Output:

Category: misc
Reference Implementation 
import base64
import hmac
from typing import Any, Union  # Standard library
import numpy as np  # Third-party needed for seeded random bytes

 def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
     """
     Encode the plaintext using the Base64 algorithm.
 
     Args:
         problem (dict): The problem dictionary generated by `generate_problem`.
 
     Returns:
         dict: A dictionary containing 'encoded_data'.
     
 
     NOTE: Your solution must pass validation by:
     1. Returning correctly formatted output
     2. Having no NaN or infinity values
     3. Matching expected results within numerical tolerance
     """
     plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
 
     try:
         # Encode the data using standard Base64
         encoded_data = base64.b64encode(plaintext)
         return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
 
     except Exception as e:
         raise  # Re-raise exception

import base64

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        """Optimized Base64 encoding using the standard library."""
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        encoded_data = base64.b64encode(plaintext)
        return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I'll create a Cython-optimized Base64 encoder to replace the standard base64.b64encode. The approach involves:
1. Precomputing the Base64 alphabet for fast lookups
2. Using memory views for efficient byte access
3. Handling padding cases separately
4. Compiling to C for native performance

First, I'll create the setup.py file to compile our Cython module:

edit
file: setup.py
lines: 0-0
---
from distutils.core import setup
from Cython.Build import cythonize

setup(
    ext_modules = cythonize("base64_cython.pyx")
)
---


Next, I'll implement the optimized Base64 encoder in Cython:

edit
file: base64_cython.pyx
lines: 0-0
---
cdef char alphabet[64] = "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"

def base64_encode(bytes data):
    cdef:
        const unsigned char[:] in_buf = data
        int in_len = len(data)
        int out_len = (in_len + 2) // 3 * 4
        bytearray out_buf = bytearray(out_len)
        int i, j = 0
        unsigned char a, b, c
        int chunks = in_len // 3
        int remainder = in_len % 3

    for i in range(0, chunks * 3, 3):
        a = in_buf[i]
        b = in_buf[i+1]
        c = in_buf[i+2]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
        out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)]
        out_buf[j+3] = alphabet[c & 0x3F]
        j += 4

    if remainder == 1:
        a = in_buf[chunks*3]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[(a & 0x03) << 4]
        out_buf[j+2] = 61  # '='
        out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
    elif remainder == 2:
        a = in_buf[chunks*3]
        b = in_buf[chunks*3+1]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
        out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[(b & 0x0F) << 2]
        out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='

    return bytes(out_buf)
---


Finally, I'll create the solver.py that uses our optimized encoder:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-0
---
try:
    from base64_cython import base64_encode
except ImportError:
    import base64
    base64_encode = base64.b64encode

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        try:
            encoded_data = base64_encode(plaintext)
            return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
        except Exception as e:
            raise

    cdef:
        const unsigned char[:] in_buf = data
        int in_len = len(data)
        int out_len = (in_len + 2) // 3 * 4
        bytearray out_buf = bytearray(out_len)
        int i, j = 0
        unsigned char a, b, c
        int chunks = in_len // 3
        int remainder = in_len % 3

    for i in range(0, chunks * 3, 3):
        a = in_buf[i]
        b = in_buf[i+1]
        c = in_buf[i+2]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
        out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)]
        out_buf[j+3] = alphabet[c & 0x3F]
        j += 4

    if remainder == 1:
        a = in_buf[chunks*3]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[(a & 0x03) << 4]
        out_buf[j+2] = 61  # '='

        int chunks = in_len // 3
        int remainder = in_len % 3

        a = in_buf[i]
        b = in_buf[i+1]
        c = in_buf[i+2]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
        out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)]
        out_buf[j+3] = alphabet[c & 0x3F]

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The evaluation shows our Cython implementation is slower than the standard base64.b64encode. Let's optimize the Cython code further by:
1. Using pointers instead of memory views for direct memory access
2. Precomputing the output length
3. Using a single buffer allocation
4. Optimizing the main loop

Here's the improved implementation:

edit
file: base64_cython.pyx
lines: 1-38
---
from cpython cimport PyBytes_FromStringAndSize
from libc.stdlib cimport malloc, free

cdef char* alphabet = "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"

def base64_encode(bytes data):
    cdef:
        const unsigned char* in_ptr = data
        int in_len = len(data)
        int out_len = (in_len + 2) // 3 * 4
        unsigned char* out_buf = <unsigned char*> malloc(out_len * sizeof(unsigned char))
        int i, j = 0
        unsigned char a, b, c
        int chunks = in_len // 3
        int remainder = in_len % 3
    
    if out_buf is NULL:
        raise MemoryError()
    
    # Process full chunks
    for i in range(chunks):
        a = in_ptr[0]
        b = in_ptr[1]
        c = in_ptr[2]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
        out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)]
        out_buf[j+3] = alphabet[c & 0x3F]
        in_ptr += 3
        j += 4

    # Process remainder
    if remainder == 1:
        a = in_ptr[0]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[(a & 0x03) << 4]
        out_buf[j+2] = 61  # '='
        out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
    elif remainder == 2:
        a = in_ptr[0]
        b = in_ptr[1]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
        out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[(b & 0x0F) << 2]
        out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
    
    cdef bytes result = PyBytes_FromStringAndSize(<char*>out_buf, out_len)
    free(out_buf)
    return result

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
We're getting a 6% improvement, but we can do better. Let's optimize further by:
1. Using loop unrolling to process 4 chunks (12 bytes) at a time
2. Removing the chunks variable and using pointer arithmetic directly
3. Using a precomputed lookup table for the main encoding

Here's the optimized version:

edit
file: base64_cython.pyx
lines: 1-49
---
# distutils: extra_compile_args = -O3 -march=native

from cpython cimport PyBytes_FromStringAndSize
from libc.stdlib cimport malloc, free
cimport cython

cdef char* alphabet = "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"

@cython.boundscheck(False)
@cython.wraparound(False)
def base64_encode(bytes data):
    cdef:
        const unsigned char* in_ptr = data
        int in_len = len(data)
        int out_len = (in_len + 2) // 3 * 4
        unsigned char* out_buf = <unsigned char*> malloc(out_len * sizeof(unsigned char))
        int i, j = 0
        unsigned char a, b, c
        int chunks = in_len // 3
        int remainder = in_len % 3
    
    if out_buf is NULL:
        raise MemoryError()
    
    # Process 4 chunks at a time
    cdef int unrolled_chunks = chunks // 4
    cdef int remaining_chunks = chunks % 4
    
    for i in range(unrolled_chunks):
        # Process 12 bytes (4 chunks)
        for _ in range(4):
            a = in_ptr[0]
            b = in_ptr[1]
            c = in_ptr[2]
            out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
            out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
            out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)]
            out_buf[j+3] = alphabet[c & 0x3F]
            in_ptr += 3
            j += 4
    
    # Process remaining chunks
    for i in range(remaining_chunks):
        a = in_ptr[0]
        b = in_ptr[1]
        c = in_ptr[2]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
        out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)]
        out_buf[j+3] = alphabet[c & 0x3F]
        in_ptr += 3
        j += 4

    # Process remainder
    if remainder == 1:
        a = in_ptr[0]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[(a & 0x03) << 4]
        out_buf[j+2] = 61  # '='
        out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
    elif remainder == 2:
        a = in_ptr[0]
        b = in_ptr[1]
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
        out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[(b & 0x0F) << 2]
        out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
    
    cdef bytes result = PyBytes_FromStringAndSize(<char*>out_buf, out_len)
    free(out_buf)
    return result

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The parallelization attempt didn't improve performance, likely due to the overhead of thread management. Let's try a different approach using a precomputed lookup table for all possible 3-byte combinations. This will trade memory for speed by storing all possible base64 encodings for 3-byte sequences.

edit
file: base64_cython.pyx
lines: 1-71
---
# distutils: extra_compile_args = -O3 -march=native

from cpython cimport PyBytes_FromStringAndSize
from libc.stdlib cimport malloc, free
cimport cython

# Precompute lookup table for all 3-byte combinations
cdef unsigned char* lookup_table = <unsigned char*> malloc(256 * 256 * 256 * 4 * sizeof(unsigned char))
cdef char* alphabet = "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"

# Initialize lookup table
cdef int i, j, k, idx
cdef unsigned char a, b, c
for i in range(256):
    for j in range(256):
        for k in range(256):
            idx = (i << 16) | (j << 8) | k
            lookup_table[idx*4] = alphabet[i >> 2]
            lookup_table[idx*4+1] = alphabet[((i & 0x03) << 4) | (j >> 4)]
            lookup_table[idx*4+2] = alphabet[((j & 0x0F) << 2) | (k >> 6)]
            lookup_table[idx*4+3] = alphabet[k & 0x3F]

@cython.boundscheck(False)
@cython.wraparound(False)
def base64_encode(bytes data):
    cdef:
        const unsigned char* in_ptr = data
        int in_len = len(data)
        int out_len = (in_len + 2) // 3 * 4
        unsigned char* out_buf = <unsigned char*> malloc(out_len * sizeof(unsigned char))
        int chunks = in_len // 3
        int remainder = in_len % 3
        int i, j = 0
        unsigned int triplet
    
    if out_buf is NULL:
        raise MemoryError()
    
    # Process full chunks using lookup table
    for i in range(chunks):
        triplet = (in_ptr[0] << 16) | (in_ptr[1] << 8) | in_ptr[2]
        out_buf[j] = lookup_table[triplet*4]
        out_buf[j+1] = lookup_table[triplet*4+1]
        out_buf[j+2] = lookup_table[triplet*4+2]
        out_buf[j+3] = lookup_table[triplet*4+3]
        in_ptr += 3
        j += 4

    # Process remainder
    if remainder == 1:
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[in_ptr[0] >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[(in_ptr[0] & 0x03) << 4]
        out_buf[j+2] = 61  # '='
        out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
    elif remainder == 2:
        out_buf[j] = alphabet[in_ptr[0] >> 2]
        out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((in_ptr[0] & 0x03) << 4) | (in_ptr[1] >> 4)]
        out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[(in_ptr[1] & 0x0F) << 2]
        out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
    
    cdef bytes result = PyBytes_FromStringAndSize(<char*>out_buf, out_len)
    free(out_buf)
    return result

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The lookup table approach was too slow due to the massive initialization time. Let's try a different optimization by using SIMD instructions with the `numba` package. This will allow us to vectorize the encoding process and process multiple chunks simultaneously.

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-14
---
import numpy as np
import numba
import base64

@numba.njit
def base64_encode_numba(data):
    alphabet = "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"
    in_len = len(data)
    out_len = (in_len + 2) // 3 * 4
    out_buf = bytearray(out_len)
    chunks = in_len // 3
    remainder = in_len % 3
    j = 0
    
    # Process full chunks
    for i in range(chunks):
        a = data[i*3]
        b = data[i*3+1]
        c = data[i*3+2]
        out_buf[j] = ord(alphabet[a >> 2])
        out_buf[j+1] = ord(alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)])
        out_buf[j+2] = ord(alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)])
        out_buf[j+3] = ord(alphabet[c & 0x3F])
        j += 4

    # Process remainder
    if remainder == 1:
        a = data[chunks*3]
        out_buf[j] = ord(alphabet[a >> 2])
        out_buf[j+1] = ord(alphabet[(a & 0x03) << 4])
        out_buf[j+2] = ord('=')
        out_buf[j+3] = ord('=')
    elif remainder == 2:
        a = data[chunks*3]
        b = data[chunks*3+1]
        out_buf[j] = ord(alphabet[a >> 2])
        out_buf[j+1] = ord(alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)])
        out_buf[j+2] = ord(alphabet[(b & 0x0F) << 2])
        out_buf[j+3] = ord('=')
    
    return bytes(out_buf)

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        try:
            # Convert bytes to numpy array for numba optimization
            data = np.frombuffer(plaintext, dtype=np.uint8)
            encoded_data = base64_encode_numba(data)
            return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
        except Exception as e:
            # Fallback to standard base64
            return {"encoded_data": base64.b64encode(plaintext)}
---

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The lookup table approach had high initialization costs, and the numba implementation didn't provide significant speedup. Let's try a different approach using PyPy's JIT capabilities by writing a pure Python implementation that can be optimized by PyPy's JIT compiler. This avoids the overhead of Cython compilation and numba JIT compilation.

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-53
---
import base64

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        try:
            # PyPy-optimized Base64 encoder
            alphabet = "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"
            in_len = len(plaintext)
            out_len = (in_len + 2) // 3 * 4
            out_buf = bytearray(out_len)
            chunks = in_len // 3
            remainder = in_len % 3
            j = 0
            
            # Process full chunks
            for i in range(chunks):
                # Access bytes directly using slicing
                a = plaintext[i*3]
                b = plaintext[i*3+1]
                c = plaintext[i*3+2]
                out_buf[j] = ord(alphabet[a >> 2])
                out_buf[j+1] = ord(alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)])
                out_buf[j+2] = ord(alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)])
                out_buf[j+3] = ord(alphabet[c & 0x3F])
                j += 4

            # Process remainder
            if remainder == 1:
                a = plaintext[chunks*3]
                out_buf[j] = ord(alphabet[a >> 2])
                out_buf[j+1] = ord(alphabet[(a & 0x03) << 4])
                out_buf[j+2] = ord('=')
                out_buf[j+3] = ord('=')
            elif remainder == 2:
                a = plaintext[chunks*3]
                b = plaintext[chunks*3+1]
                out_buf[j] = ord(alphabet[a >> 2])
                out_buf[j+1] = ord(alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)])
                out_buf[j+2] = ord(alphabet[(b & 0x0F) << 2])
                out_buf[j+3] = ord('=')
            
            return {"encoded_data": bytes(out_buf)}
        except Exception as e:
            # Fallback to standard base64
            return {"encoded_data": base64.b64encode(plaintext)}

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
It seems the pure Python implementation is timing out for larger inputs. Let's go back to the Cython approach but with a more optimized implementation. I'll create a new Cython implementation that avoids memory allocations by using a preallocated buffer and optimizes the main loop with loop unrolling.

edit
file: base64_cython.pyx
lines: 1-63
---
# distutils: extra_compile_args = -O3 -march=native -flto

from cpython cimport PyBytes_FromStringAndSize
from libc.stdlib cimport malloc, free
cimport cython

cdef char* alphabet = "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"

@cython.boundscheck(False)
@cython.wraparound(False)
cdef void base64_encode_chunk(const unsigned char* in_ptr, unsigned char* out_buf) nogil:
    cdef unsigned char a = in_ptr[0]
    cdef unsigned char b = in_ptr[1]
    cdef unsigned char c = in_ptr[2]
    out_buf[0] = alphabet[a >> 2]
    out_buf[1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
    out_buf[2] = alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)]
    out_buf[3] = alphabet[c & 0x3F]

def base64_encode(bytes data):
    cdef:
        const unsigned char* in_ptr = data
        int in_len = len(data)
        int out_len = (in_len + 2) // 3 * 4
        unsigned char* out_buf = <unsigned char*> malloc(out_len * sizeof(unsigned char))
        int chunks = in_len // 3
        int remainder = in_len % 3
        int i, j = 0
    
    if out_buf is NULL:
        raise MemoryError()
    
    # Process chunks in groups of 8 for better cache utilization
    cdef int group_size = 8
    cdef int groups = chunks // group_size
    cdef int remaining_chunks = chunks % group_size
    
    with nogil:
        # Process groups of 8 chunks (24 bytes)
        for i in range(groups):
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr, out_buf + j)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 3, out_buf + j + 4)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 6, out_buf + j + 8)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 9, out_buf + j + 12)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 12, out_buf + j + 16)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 15, out_buf + j + 20)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 18, out_buf + j + 24)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 21, out_buf + j + 28)
            in_ptr += 24
            j += 32
        
        # Process remaining chunks
        for i in range(remaining_chunks):
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr, out_buf + j)
            in_ptr += 3
            j += 4

        # Process remainder
        if remainder == 1:
            out_buf[j] = alphabet[in_ptr[0] >> 2]
            out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[(in_ptr[0] & 0x03) << 4]
            out_buf[j+2] = 61  # '='
            out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
        elif remainder == 2:
            out_buf[j] = alphabet[in_ptr[0] >> 2]
            out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((in_ptr[0] & 0x03) << 4) | (in_ptr[1] >> 4)]
            out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[(in_ptr[1] & 0x0F) << 2]
            out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
    
    cdef bytes result = PyBytes_FromStringAndSize(<char*>out_buf, out_len)
    free(out_buf)
    return result

import base64
from base64_cython import base64_encode

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        try:
            # Use our optimized Cython encoder
            encoded_data = base64_encode(plaintext)
            return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
        except Exception as e:
            # Fallback to standard base64
            return {"encoded_data": base64.b64encode(plaintext)}

# distutils: extra_compile_args = -O3 -march=native -flto

from cpython cimport PyBytes_FromStringAndSize
from libc.stdlib cimport malloc, free
cimport cython

cdef char* alphabet = "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"

@cython.boundscheck(False)
@cython.wraparound(False)
cdef void base64_encode_chunk(const unsigned char* in_ptr, unsigned char* out_buf) nogil:
    cdef unsigned char a = in_ptr[0]
    cdef unsigned char b = in_ptr[1]
    cdef unsigned char c = in_ptr[2]
    out_buf[0] = alphabet[a >> 2]
    out_buf[1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
    out_buf[2] = alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)]
    out_buf[3] = alphabet[c & 0x3F]

def base64_encode(bytes data):
    cdef:
        const unsigned char* in_ptr = data
        int in_len = len(data)
        int out_len = (in_len + 2) // 3 * 4
        unsigned char* out_buf = <unsigned char*> malloc(out_len * sizeof(unsigned char))
        int chunks = in_len // 3
        int remainder = in_len % 3
        int i, j = 0
    
    if out_buf is NULL:
        raise MemoryError()
    
    # Process chunks in groups of 8 for better cache utilization
    cdef int group_size = 8
    cdef int groups = chunks // group_size
    cdef int remaining_chunks = chunks % group_size
    
    with nogil:
        # Process groups of 8 chunks (24 bytes)
        for i in range(groups):
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr, out_buf + j)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 3, out_buf + j + 4)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 6, out_buf + j + 8)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 9, out_buf + j + 12)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 12, out_buf + j + 16)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 15, out_buf + j + 20)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 18, out_buf + j + 24)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 21, out_buf + j + 28)
            in_ptr += 24
            j += 32
        
        # Process remaining chunks
        for i in range(remaining_chunks):
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr, out_buf + j)
            in_ptr += 3
            j += 4

        # Process remainder
        if remainder == 1:
            out_buf[j] = alphabet[in_ptr[0] >> 2]
            out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[(in_ptr[0] & 0x03) << 4]
            out_buf[j+2] = 61  # '='

            out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
    
    cdef bytes result = PyBytes_FromStringAndSize(<char*>out_buf, out_len)
    free(out_buf)
    return result

import base64
from base64_cython import base64_encode

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        try:
            # Use our optimized Cython encoder
            encoded_data = base64_encode(plaintext)
            return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
        except Exception as e:
            # Fallback to standard base64
            return {"encoded_data": base64.b64encode(plaintext)}

# distutils: extra_compile_args = -O3 -march=native -flto

from cpython cimport PyBytes_FromStringAndSize
from libc.stdlib cimport malloc, free
cimport cython

cdef char* alphabet = "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"

@cython.boundscheck(False)
@cython.wraparound(False)
cdef void base64_encode_chunk(const unsigned char* in_ptr, unsigned char* out_buf) nogil:
    cdef unsigned char a = in_ptr[0]
    cdef unsigned char b = in_ptr[1]
    cdef unsigned char c = in_ptr[2]
    out_buf[0] = alphabet[a >> 2]
    out_buf[1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
    out_buf[2] = alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)]
    out_buf[3] = alphabet[c & 0x3F]

def base64_encode(bytes data):
    cdef:
        const unsigned char* in_ptr = data
        int in_len = len(data)
        int out_len = (in_len + 2) // 3 * 4
        unsigned char* out_buf = <unsigned char*> malloc(out_len * sizeof(unsigned char))
        int chunks = in_len // 3
        int remainder = in_len % 3
        int i, j = 0
    
    if out_buf is NULL:
        raise MemoryError()
    
    # Process chunks in groups of 8 for better cache utilization
    cdef int group_size = 8
    cdef int groups = chunks // group_size
    cdef int remaining_chunks = chunks % group_size
    
    with nogil:
        # Process groups of 8 chunks (24 bytes)
        for i in range(groups):
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr, out_buf + j)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 3, out_buf + j + 4)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 6, out_buf + j + 8)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 9, out_buf + j + 12)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 12, out_buf + j + 16)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 15, out_buf + j + 20)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 18, out_buf + j + 24)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 21, out_buf + j + 28)
            in_ptr += 24
            j += 32
        
        # Process remaining chunks
        for i in range(remaining_chunks):
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr, out_buf + j)
            in_ptr += 3
            j += 4

        # Process remainder
        if remainder == 1:
            out_buf[j] = alphabet[in_ptr[0] >> 2]
            out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[(in_ptr[0] & 0x03) << 4]
            out_buf[j+2] = 61  # '='
            out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
        elif remainder == 2:
            out_buf[j] = alphabet[in_ptr[0] >> 2]
            out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((in_ptr[0] & 0x03) << 4) | (in_ptr[1] >> 4)]
            out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[(in_ptr[1] & 0x0F) << 2]
            out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
    
    cdef bytes result = PyBytes_FromStringAndSize(<char*>out_buf, out_len)
    free(out_buf)
    return result

Now I'll create the optimized implementation:

file: base64_cython.pyx
lines: 0-0
---
# distutils: extra_compile_args = -O3 -march=native -flto

from cpython cimport PyBytes_FromStringAndSize
from libc.stdlib cimport malloc, free
cimport cython

cdef char* alphabet = "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"

@cython.boundscheck(False)
@cython.wraparound(False)
cdef void base64_encode_chunk(const unsigned char* in_ptr, unsigned char* out_buf) nogil:
    cdef unsigned char a = in_ptr[0]
    cdef unsigned char b = in_ptr[1]
    cdef unsigned char c = in_ptr[2]
    out_buf[0] = alphabet[a >> 2]
    out_buf[1] = alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
    out_buf[2] = alphabet[((b & 0x0F) << 2) | (c >> 6)]
    out_buf[3] = alphabet[c & 0x3F]

def base64_encode(bytes data):
    cdef:
        const unsigned char* in_ptr = data
        int in_len = len(data)
        int out_len = (in_len + 2) // 3 * 4
        unsigned char* out_buf = <unsigned char*> malloc(out_len * sizeof(unsigned char))
        int chunks = in_len // 3
        int remainder = in_len % 3
        int i, j = 0
    
    if out_buf is NULL:
        raise MemoryError()
    
    # Process chunks in groups of 8 for better cache utilization
    cdef int group_size = 8
    cdef int groups = chunks // group_size
    cdef int remaining_chunks = chunks % group_size
    
    with nogil:
        # Process groups of 8 chunks (24 bytes)
        for i in range(groups):
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr, out_buf + j)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 3, out_buf + j + 4)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 6, out_buf + j + 8)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 9, out_buf + j + 12)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 12, out_buf + j + 16)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 15, out_buf + j + 20)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 18, out_buf + j + 24)
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr + 21, out_buf + j + 28)
            in_ptr += 24
            j += 32
        
        # Process remaining chunks
        for i in range(remaining_chunks):
            base64_encode_chunk(in_ptr, out_buf + j)
            in_ptr += 3
            j += 4

        # Process remainder
        if remainder == 1:
            out_buf[j] = alphabet[in_ptr[0] >> 2]
            out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[(in_ptr[0] & 0x03) << 4]
            out_buf[j+2] = 61  # '='
            out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
        elif remainder == 2:
            out_buf[j] = alphabet[in_ptr[0] >> 2]
            out_buf[j+1] = alphabet[((in_ptr[0] & 0x03) << 4) | (in_ptr[1] >> 4)]
            out_buf[j+2] = alphabet[(in_ptr[1] & 0x0F) << 2]
            out_buf[j+3] = 61  # '='
    
    cdef bytes result = PyBytes_FromStringAndSize(<char*>out_buf, out_len)
    free(out_buf)
    return result

IMPORTANT: Each set of triple backticks (```) must always be on their own line, without any other words or anything else on that line.

Here are the commands available to you. Ensure you include one and only one of the following commands in each of your responses:
- `edit`: Replace a range of lines with new content in a file. This is how you can create files: if the file does not exist, it will be created. Here is an example:
```
edit
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

Example:
edit
file: solver.py
lines: 5-7
---
def improved_function():
print("Optimized solution")
---
- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I'll create a pure Python implementation of Base64 encoding that's optimized for performance. The key optimizations include:
1. Precomputing the alphabet as a bytes object for direct indexing
2. Processing input in aligned chunks to minimize condition checks
3. Using bitwise operations for efficient encoding
4. Preallocating the output buffer to avoid resizing

Here's the implementation:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-1000
---
class Solver:
    def base64_encode(self, data: bytes) -> bytes:
        if not data:
            return b""
        
        alphabet = b"ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"
        length = len(data)
        # Calculate output length: 4 * ceil(len/3)
        out_len = (length + 2) // 3 * 4
        out = bytearray(out_len)
        
        # Process full triplets
        i = 0
        j = 0
        while i + 2 < length:
            # Pack 3 bytes into 24-bit integer
            n = (data[i] << 16) | (data[i+1] << 8) | data[i+2]
            
            # Split into 4 indices (6 bits each)
            out[j] = alphabet[(n >> 18) & 0x3F]
            out[j+1] = alphabet[(n >> 12) & 0x3F]
            out[j+2] = alphabet[(n >> 6) & 0x3F]
            out[j+3] = alphabet[n & 0x3F]
            
            i += 3
            j += 4
        
        # Handle remaining bytes (0, 1, or 2 bytes)
        remaining = length - i
        if remaining == 2:
            n = (data[i] << 16) | (data[i+1] << 8)
            out[j] = alphabet[(n >> 18) & 0x3F]
            out[j+1] = alphabet[(n >> 12) & 0x3F]
            out[j+2] = alphabet[(n >> 6) & 0x3F]
            out[j+3] = 61  # '=' character
        elif remaining == 1:
            n = data[i] << 16
            out[j] = alphabet[(n >> 18) & 0x3F]
            out[j+1] = alphabet[(n >> 12) & 0x3F]
            out[j+2] = 61  # '='
            out[j+3] = 61  # '='
        
        return bytes(out)

    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        try:
            encoded_data = self.base64_encode(plaintext)
            return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
        except Exception as e:
            raise
---

            out[j+1] = alphabet[(n >> 12) & 0x3F]
            out[j+2] = alphabet[(n >> 6) & 0x3F]
            out[j+3] = alphabet[n & 0x3F]

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The evaluation shows our pure Python implementation is timing out. Let's optimize it further by:
1. Using local variables to reduce attribute lookups
2. Removing redundant condition checks
3. Using integer arithmetic instead of bitwise operations where possible
4. Precomputing the padding cases

Here's the optimized version:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-1000
---
class Solver:
    def base64_encode(self, data: bytes) -> bytes:
        if not data:
            return b""
        
        alphabet = b"ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"
        length = len(data)
        out_len = (length + 2) // 3 * 4
        out = bytearray(out_len)
        i = j = 0
        
        # Process full triplets
        while i + 2 < length:
            a, b, c = data[i], data[i+1], data[i+2]
            out[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
            out[j+1] = alphabet[((a & 3) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
            out[j+2] = alphabet[((b & 15) << 2) | (c >> 6)]
            out[j+3] = alphabet[c & 63]
            i += 3
            j += 4
        
        # Handle remaining bytes
        remaining = length - i
        if remaining == 2:
            a, b = data[i], data[i+1]
            out[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
            out[j+1] = alphabet[((a & 3) << 4) | (b >> 4)]
            out[j+2] = alphabet[(b & 15) << 2]
            out[j+3] = 61  # '='
        elif remaining == 1:
            a = data[i]
            out[j] = alphabet[a >> 2]
            out[j+1] = alphabet[(a & 3) << 4]
            out[j+2] = 61  # '='
            out[j+3] = 61  # '='
        
        return bytes(out)

    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        try:
            encoded_data = self.base64_encode(plaintext)
            return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
        except Exception as e:
            raise
---

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The evaluation shows our implementation is 10% faster than the reference, but we can do better. Let's try using the binascii module which provides a lower-level Base64 implementation that might be faster:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-1000
---
import binascii

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        try:
            # Use binascii's b2a_base64 which is faster than base64.b64encode
            # Then remove the trailing newline that b2a_base64 adds
            encoded_data = binascii.b2a_base64(plaintext)[:-1]
            return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
        except Exception as e:
            raise
---

            # Use binascii's b2a_base64 which is faster than base64.b64encode
            # Then remove the trailing newline that b2a_base64 adds
            encoded_data = binascii.b2a_base64(plaintext)[:-1]
            return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
        except Exception as e:
            raise
---

Here are the commands available to you. Ensure you include one and only one of the following commands in each of your responses:
- `edit`: Replace a range of lines with new content in a file. This is how you can create files: if the file does not exist, it will be created. Here is an example:
```
edit
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

Example:
edit
file: solver.py
lines: 5-7
---
def improved_function():
print("Optimized solution")
---
- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

import base64
import numpy as np

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        # Precompute the Base64 alphabet as a numpy array for fast lookup
        self.alphabet = np.array(list("ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"), dtype='S1')
        
    def encode_chunk(self, chunk):
        """Encode a 3-byte chunk to Base64 using precomputed alphabet."""
        b1, b2, b3 = chunk
        indices = [
            b1 >> 2,
            ((b1 & 0x03) << 4) | (b2 >> 4),
            ((b2 & 0x0F) << 2) | (b3 >> 6),
            b3 & 0x3F
        ]
        return b''.join(self.alphabet[indices])
    
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        try:
            # For small inputs, use the standard library for better performance
            if len(plaintext) < 4096:
                encoded_data = base64.b64encode(plaintext)
                return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
            
            # Process in batches for large inputs
            result = bytearray()
            padding = b'=' * ((3 - len(plaintext) % 3) % 3)
            padded = plaintext + b'\x00' * (3 - len(plaintext) % 3) % 3
            
            # Process 3000 bytes at a time (1000 chunks)
            for i in range(0, len(padded), 3000):
                chunk = padded[i:i+3000]
                arr = np.frombuffer(chunk, dtype=np.uint8)
                arr = arr.reshape(-1, 3)
                for triplet in arr:
                    result.extend(self.encode_chunk(triplet))
            
            # Replace padding placeholders
            result = bytes(result).replace(b'A', b'=')[:-len(padding)] + padding
            return {"encoded_data": result}
        except Exception as e:
            raise

I see the issues in my implementation. Let me fix the padding calculation and the padding replacement logic:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-1000
---
import base64
import numpy as np

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        # Precompute the Base64 alphabet as a numpy array for fast lookup
        self.alphabet = np.array(list("ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/"), dtype='S1')
        
    def encode_chunk(self, chunk):
        """Encode a 3-byte chunk to Base64 using precomputed alphabet."""
        b1, b2, b3 = chunk
        indices = [
            b1 >> 2,
            ((b1 & 0x03) << 4) | (b2 >> 4),
            ((b2 & 0x0F) << 2) | (b3 >> 6),
            b3 & 0x3F
        ]
        return b''.join(self.alphabet[indices])
    
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        try:
            # For small inputs, use the standard library for better performance
            if len(plaintext) < 4096:
                encoded_data = base64.b64encode(plaintext)
                return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
            
            # Process in batches for large inputs
            result = bytearray()
            pad_len = (3 - len(plaintext) % 3) % 3
            padded = plaintext + b'\x00' * pad_len
            
            # Process 3000 bytes at a time (1000 chunks)
            for i in range(0, len(padded), 3000):
                chunk = padded[i:i+3000]
                arr = np.frombuffer(chunk, dtype=np.uint8)
                arr = arr.reshape(-1, 3)
                for triplet in arr:
                    result.extend(self.encode_chunk(triplet))
            
            # Calculate padding characters
            mod = len(plaintext) % 3
            if mod == 1:
                base64_pad = 2
            elif mod == 2:
                base64_pad = 1
            else:
                base64_pad = 0
                
            # Apply padding
            result_bytes = bytes(result)
            if base64_pad:
                result_bytes = result_bytes[:-base64_pad] + b'=' * base64_pad
                
            return {"encoded_data": result_bytes}
        except Exception as e:
            raise

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The previous approach had performance issues. Let's optimize further by using a precomputed lookup table for all possible 3-byte combinations, which should provide significant speed improvements for large inputs:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-1000
---
import base64

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        # Precompute lookup table for all possible 3-byte combinations
        self.lookup_table = [None] * (256 * 256 * 256)
        alphabet = b'ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/'
        
        for i in range(256):
            for j in range(256):
                for k in range(256):
                    # Compute Base64 encoding for this 3-byte combination
                    indices = [
                        i >> 2,
                        ((i & 0x03) << 4) | (j >> 4),
                        ((j & 0x0F) << 2) | (k >> 6),
                        k & 0x3F
                    ]
                    encoded = bytes(alphabet[idx] for idx in indices)
                    self.lookup_table[i * 65536 + j * 256 + k] = encoded
    
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        n = len(plaintext)
        result = bytearray()
        full_chunks = n // 3
        remainder = n % 3
        
        # Process full 3-byte chunks
        for i in range(full_chunks):
            start = i * 3
            a, b, c = plaintext[start], plaintext[start+1], plaintext[start+2]
            index = a * 65536 + b * 256 + c
            result.extend(self.lookup_table[index])
        
        # Handle remaining bytes
        if remainder == 1:
            a = plaintext[-1]
            result.append(b'ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/'[a >> 2])
            result.append(b'ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/'[(a & 0x03) << 4])
            result.extend(b'==')
        elif remainder == 2:
            a, b = plaintext[-2], plaintext[-1]
            result.append(b'ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/'[a >> 2])
            result.append(b'ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/'[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)])
            result.append(b'ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/'[((b & 0x0F) << 2)])
            result.append(ord('='))
        
        return {"encoded_data": bytes(result)}

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The lookup table approach is too memory-intensive and initialization is too slow. Let's switch to a more efficient approach using a precomputed 64-character alphabet and batch processing with bytearrays:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-1000
---
import base64

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # For small inputs, use the standard library
        if len(plaintext) < 100000:
            return {"encoded_data": base64.b64encode(plaintext)}
        
        # Precomputed base64 alphabet
        alphabet = b'ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/'
        result = bytearray()
        padding = b'=' * ((3 - len(plaintext) % 3) % 3
        padded = plaintext + b'\0' * ((3 - len(plaintext) % 3) % 3
        
        # Process 6000 bytes at a time (2000 chunks)
        for i in range(0, len(padded), 6000):
            chunk = padded[i:i+6000]
            for j in range(0, len(chunk), 3):
                # Get 3 bytes
                b1, b2, b3 = chunk[j], chunk[j+1], chunk[j+2]
                
                # Calculate indices
                idx1 = b1 >> 2
                idx2 = ((b1 & 0x03) << 4) | (b2 >> 4)
                idx3 = ((b2 & 0x0F) << 2) | (b3 >> 6)
                idx4 = b3 & 0x3F
                
                # Append characters
                result.append(alphabet[idx1])
                result.append(alphabet[idx2])
                result.append(alphabet[idx3])
                result.append(alphabet[idx4])
        
        # Apply padding
        result = bytes(result)
        if padding:
            result = result[:-len(padding)] + padding
            
        return {"encoded_data": result}
---

edit
file: solver.py

---
import base64

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        n = len(plaintext)
        # Precomputed base64 alphabet
        alphabet = b'ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789+/'
        result = bytearray()
        
        # Process full 3-byte chunks
        for i in range(0, n - n % 3, 3):
            # Get 3 bytes
            b1, b2, b3 = plaintext[i], plaintext[i+1], plaintext[i+2]
            
            # Calculate indices
            idx1 = b1 >> 2
            idx2 = ((b1 & 0x03) << 4) | (b2 >> 4)
            idx3 = ((b2 & 0x0F) << 2) | (b3 >> 6)
            idx4 = b3 & 0x3F
            
            # Append characters
            result.append(alphabet[idx1])
            result.append(alphabet[idx2])
            result.append(alphabet[idx3])
            result.append(alphabet[idx4])
        
        # Handle remaining bytes
        remainder = n % 3
        if remainder == 1:
            a = plaintext[-1]
            result.append(alphabet[a >> 2])
            result.append(alphabet[(a & 0x03) << 4])
            result.extend(b'==')
        elif remainder == 2:
            a, b = plaintext[-2], plaintext[-1]
            result.append(alphabet[a >> 2])
            result.append(alphabet[((a & 0x03) << 4) | (b >> 4)])
            result.append(alphabet[(b & 0x0F) << 2])
            result.append(ord('='))
        
        return {"encoded_data": bytes(result)}

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):

file: solver.py

---
import binascii

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # binascii.b2a_base64 adds a newline, so we need to remove it
        encoded = binascii.b2a_base64(plaintext)[:-1]
        return {"encoded_data": encoded}

- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

file: solver.py
lines: 1-1000
---
import binascii

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # binascii.b2a_base64 is faster than base64.b64encode
        encoded = binascii.b2a_base64(plaintext)
        # Remove trailing newline to match base64.b64encode output
        return {"encoded_data": encoded.rstrip(b'
')}
---

file: solver.py

---
import binascii

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # binascii.b2a_base64 is faster than base64.b64encode
        encoded = binascii.b2a_base64(plaintext)
        # Remove trailing newline to match base64.b64encode output
        return {"encoded_data": encoded.rstrip(b'
')}

lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

file: solver.py

import binascii

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # binascii.b2a_base64 is faster than base64.b64encode
        encoded = binascii.b2a_base64(plaintext)
        # Remove trailing newline to match base64.b64encode output
        return {"encoded_data": encoded.rstrip(b'
')}

- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

import binascii

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        """Optimized Base64 encoding using binascii for better performance."""
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Use binascii.b2a_base64 which is faster than base64.b64encode
        # Remove trailing newline (b2a_base64 adds a newline by default)
        encoded_data = binascii.b2a_base64(plaintext, newline=False)
        return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
---

Remember to sandwich your command in between ``` and ```.
IMPORTANT: Each set of triple backticks (```) must always be on their own line, without any other words or anything else on that line.

Here are the commands available to you. Ensure you include one and only one of the following commands in each of your responses:
- `edit`: Replace a range of lines with new content in a file. This is how you can create files: if the file does not exist, it will be created. Here is an example:
```
edit
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

Example:
edit
file: solver.py
lines: 5-7
---
def improved_function():
print("Optimized solution")
---
- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

file: solver.py
lines: 1-9999
---
import binascii

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        """Optimized Base64 encoding using binascii for better performance."""
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Use binascii.b2a_base64 which is faster than base64.b64encode
        # Remove trailing newline (b2a_base64 adds a newline by default)
        encoded_data = binascii.b2a_base64(plaintext, newline=False)
        return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
---

edit
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

Example:
edit
file: solver.py
lines: 5-7
---
def improved_function():
print("Optimized solution")
---
- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

import base64

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        """Optimized Base64 encoding using the standard library."""
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Use standard base64.b64encode which is highly optimized
        encoded_data = base64.b64encode(plaintext)
        return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}

IMPORTANT: Each set of triple backticks (```) must always be on their own line, without any other words or anything else on that line.

Here are the commands available to you. Ensure you include one and only one of the following commands in each of your responses:
- `edit`: Replace a range of lines with new content in a file. This is how you can create files: if the file does not exist, it will be created. Here is an example:
```
edit
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

Example:
edit
file: solver.py
lines: 5-7
---
def improved_function():
print("Optimized solution")
---
- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

import base64

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        """Optimized Base64 encoding using the standard library."""
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        encoded_data = base64.b64encode(plaintext)
        return {"encoded_data": encoded_data}
